                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-90767666717">
                      Big Shrimpin': The Runaway Success of 'Forrest Gump,' by the Numbers
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-90767666717" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="D-b Fs-n Pb-14 byline col">
                           <span class="D-b author-name col-left">
                            <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/movies/author/meriah-doty" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/movies/author/meriah-doty" rel="author" style="color:#000;">
                             Meriah Doty
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <span class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n author-title">
                            Editor
                           </span>
                           <time class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n date">
                            <span>
                             July 4, 2014
                            </span>
                           </time>
                           <div class="follow Mt-4">
                            <iframe allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets/follow_button.html?screen_name=meriahonfiah&amp;show_screen_name=false&amp;show_count=false" style="border:none;overflow:hidden;width:60px;height:20px;">

                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t Va-b" style="width:133px;">
                          <a class="attribution-photo author-photo-link col" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/movies/author/meriah-doty" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/movies/author/meriah-doty">
                           <img alt="Meriah Doty" class="author-photo" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w133/0eea22f1df14140ee1e171586211a8f8accb97c2.png" style="width:133px;"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>

                       </div>
                      </div>

                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-90767666717" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Big Shrimpin': The Runaway Success of 'Forrest Gump,' by the Numbers" height="1372" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w2048/a14dd0069c775b96544168f65fd7248e38982fbf.jpg" width="2048"/>
                          <em>
                           Forrest Gump
                          </em>
                           the Oscar-winning, catchphrase-coining,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/movies/when-forrest-gump-stumbled-into-the-90s-culture-wars-90475343717.html" target="_blank">
                           culturally divisive
                          </a>
                          box-office hit  turns 20 years old this weekend. To celebrate, we broke down the film (and its impact) by the numbers:
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of hours it took Tom Hanks to agree to the part after reading the script:
                          <strong>
                           1.5.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of different blue checkered shirts Forrest wears: Approximately
                          <strong>
                           15.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of chocolates in Forrest's
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.russellstover.com/jump.jsp?itemType=PRODUCT&amp;itemID=900" target="_blank">
                           box of Russell Stover's
                          </a>
                          :
                          <strong>
                           34
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Forrest Gump" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/original/_-Xc-gQd5T51P3m5JaU1arlpipE.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          Length of Forrest's run across America:
                          <strong>
                           3
                          </strong>
                          years,
                          <strong>
                           2
                          </strong>
                          months,
                          <strong>
                           14
                          </strong>
                          days, and
                          <strong>
                           16
                          </strong>
                          hours.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Nike" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/40896b0b6b5669ac6f82dec51904bf5e3d6e8e3e.jpg" height="284" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                          Current price of a pair of Forrest's favorite running shoes, the
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://homiegear.bigcartel.com/product/nike-cortez" target="_blank">
                           Nike Cortez
                          </a>
                          :
                          <strong>
                           $59.99
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Tom Hanks" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w1024/c720b14602601e656117ec4771fed32580b88008.jpg" height="680" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="1024"/>
                          Age difference betweenHanks and Sally Field, who played Forrest's mother:
                          <strong>
                           10
                          </strong>
                          <strong>
                           years.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of times Forrest says "Mama":
                          <strong>
                           About
                          </strong>
                          <strong>
                           30
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <iframe allowfullscreen="true" data-src="https://movies.yahoo.com/video/marry-060000058.html?format=embed&amp;player_autoplay=false" height="393.75" width="700">
                          </iframe>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of times Forrest says "Jenny":
                          <strong>
                           About30
                          </strong>
                          (He loves them equally!)
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of times Bubba says "shrimp" in his first three minutes on-screen:
                          <strong>
                           21.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Forrest Gump" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w599/eb1207f9f6d8561ebd0b661e6d982e3c7cb72a43.jpg" height="633" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="599"/>
                          Number of handmade
                          <em>
                           Forrest Gump
                          </em>
                          -inspireditems we found on sale this week:
                          <strong>
                           175
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Haley Joel Osment Forrest Gump" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/original/MFUpKlPGsfMupI2svFeZCqYyUZc.gif" height="268" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="630"/>
                          Age ofHaley Joel Osment when he played Forrest Junior:
                          <strong>
                           5 years old
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of songs by the Doors in the film's end credits:
                          <strong>
                           5
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           Number of visual-effects shots:
                          </span>
                          <strong>
                           120,
                          </strong>
                          including the famous feather.
                          <span>
                           <br/>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <iframe data-src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/JSEdBNslGOk?rel=0" height="315" width="560">
                          </iframe>
                          Number ofU.S. presidents Forrest meets in the film:
                          <strong>
                           3.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of weeks
                          <em>
                           Forrest Gump
                          </em>
                          ran in theaters:
                          <strong>
                           42
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           Forrest Gump
                          </em>
                          'sworldwide box-office take:
                          <strong>
                           $677.4 million
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of copies
                          <em>
                           Forrest Gump
                          </em>
                          sold on home video within two months of release:
                          <strong>
                           Nearly
                          </strong>
                          <strong>
                           10 million
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of Oscars won by
                          <em>
                           Forrest Gump
                          </em>
                          :
                          <strong>
                           6
                          </strong>
                          , including Best Picture and Best Actor.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of copies the
                          <em>
                           Gump
                          </em>
                          soundtrack sold in the U.S.:
                          <strong>
                           6 million.
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Forrest Gump ping pong" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w864/7d21f66f11bad47eaf61993c894b0f531d66b171.jpg" height="628" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="864"/>
                          Number of actual U.S. table-tennis Olympic medals in real life:
                          <strong>
                           0
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.bubbagump.com/locations/" target="_blank">
                           Bubba Gump restaurants
                          </a>
                          worldwide:
                          <strong>
                           41
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <iframe allowfullscreen="true" data-src="https://movies.yahoo.com/video/boat-060000139.html?format=embed&amp;player_autoplay=false" height="393.75" width="700">
                          </iframe>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of years
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:fb68f21a-eef6-3267-8213-3c602448e3e5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.ltdanband.com/#latest-news" target="_blank">
                           Gary Sinese and the Lt. Dan Band
                          </a>
                          have been playing:
                          <strong>
                           11
                          </strong>
                          .
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Number of times you've heard someone repeat the phrase "Life is like a box of chocolates" in the last two decades:
                          <strong>

                          </strong>

Robbins and Morgan Freeman in &#x2018;The Shawshank Redemption&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETwenty years ago, on Oct. 14, 1994, Quentin Tarantino&#x2019;s game-changer \u003Cem\u003E Pulp Fiction\u003C\u002Fem\u003E hit theaters. The same day also saw the wide release of a movie that &#x2014; while overlooked at the time and grossing a fraction of \u003Cem\u003EFiction\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&apos;s box office &#x2014; might have had an arguably bigger impact among movie fans long term. It&apos;s a film that currently stands at the top of the IMDb&#x2019;s \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.imdb.com\u002Fchart\u002Ftop\"\u003Euser-voted Top 250 films\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2014; higher than \u003Cem\u003EThe Godfather\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, \u003Cem\u003EThe Empire Strikes Back\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, and yes, even \u003Cem\u003EPulp Fiction\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. That movie? \u003Cem\u003EThe Shawshank Redemption\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. How did a film initially ignored by so many people become such a phenomenon?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EFrank Darabont&#x2019;s directorial debut, which details the prison-yard friendship of wrongly convicted accountant Andy (Tim Robbins) and hardened lifer Red (Morgan Freeman), was greeted with reviews that were decent, but hardly the kind you&#x2019;d expect for a classic-in-the-making. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ew.com\u002Few\u002Farticle\u002F0,,303774,00.html\"\u003EEntertainment Weekly\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2019;s Owen Gleiberman, for instance, gave the film a B-, noting the &#x201C;brazenly mechanical plotting and its wish-fulfillment finale.&#x201D; Audiences were slow to catch on, with the film \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fboxofficemojo.com\u002Fmovies\u002F?id=shawshankredemption.htm\"\u003Eultimately grossing only $28 million\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a large chunk of which came only after the movie was nominated for seven Academy Awards including Best Picture. After it failed to win any Oscars, it wouldn&#x2019;t have been surprising if \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E had faded as a respectable memory.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYet by the time it was released on video in 1995, it proved an unlikely smash, one of the most popular video rentals of the year with more than 300,000 copies shipped. It later became a cable TV staple, with TNT airing it roughly every two months \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fonline.wsj.com\u002Fnews\u002Farticles\u002FSB10001424052702304536104579560021265554240\"\u003Efrom 1997 onwards\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Critic Andre Mouchard \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.webcitation.org\u002F5oxDybfiJ\"\u003Esuggested that the film&#x2019;s episodic structure\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which follows Andy and Red through the years starting in the 1940s, actually helped it play particularly well on television: &#x201C;Films like \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&#x2026; can deliver their punchy message every few minutes, not unlike network shows.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe coming of the Internet age helped nurture the film&#x2019;s fanbase. Even before \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E made it to cable TV, now-influential movie site IMDb had launched, and from its earliest days, the film was among the site&#x2019;s favored titles. In the first recorded Top 250 movies list in April 1996, the film was No. 2 behind only&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003EStar Wars\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, and it has never dropped below fourth place in the years that followed. Since August 2008, it has held the top slot continuously, with nearly 1.3 million voters helping it to a huge score of 9.2 out of 10. (That&#x2019;s even more impressive when you consider that it&#x2019;s a statistically weighted number, with only the votes of &#x2018;regular users&#x2019; of the site counting toward the ranking).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERELATED:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fmovies\u002F13-things-you-didn-t-c1409949868479.html\"\u003E13 Things You Didn&#x2019;t Know About &#x2018;The Shawshank Redemption&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E That said, the film&#x2019;s IMDb placing seems to be a symptom rather than a cause of its popularity. Though the site is now firmly part of the mainstream &#x2014; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.alexa.com\u002Ftopsites\u002Fglobal;1\"\u003Eone of the top 50 in the world according to the Alexa index\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2014; it was initially a small, cultish site for cinephiles, and that&#x2019;s reflected in the votes that \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E has received. The film only reached 100,000 votes in 2003 and crossed the million mark this year, long after it became a phenomenon on home video and TV. The consistent high placing certainly helped the film&apos;s cult grow over the years, but it&apos;s likely a reflection of a popularity that was already in place.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHow could a film that&#x2019;s now this popular get off to such a slow start in the first place? In reality, it was always a tricky movie to market. In contrast with the years&#x2019; other big feel-good hit, \u003Cem\u003EForrest Gump\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, it had a totally unknown director and was led by two actors who were familiar, but hardly big draws. Though \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E was based on a novella by horror writer Stephen King, it had no real genre elements, and it was both harsh (featuring among other things, prison rape and suicide) and sentimental.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERELATED:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fmovies\u002Fwhen-forrest-gump-stumbled-into-the-90s-culture-wars-90475343717.html\"\u003EWhen &#x2018;Forrest Gump&#x2019; Stumbled Into the &#x2019;90s Culture Wars\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd yet it might be the very juxtaposition of those two elements that made it endure. The studio, Columbia Pictures, couldn&#x2019;t find a way to sell the movie to audiences, perhaps because it wasn&#x2019;t sure which audience to aim it at. But once the buzz caught on thanks to the Oscar nominations and the home-video release, viewers responded to that mix of hope and brutality. \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E was the weepie that it was OK for guys to like &#x2014; it&#x2019;s frequently cited as \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ew.com\u002Few\u002Fgallery\u002F0,,20015186_20016841,00.html\"\u003Ea movie that makes men cry\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;and a recent \u003Cem\u003EVanity Fair\u003C\u002Fem\u003E piece on the production described it as \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.vanityfair.com\u002Fvf-hollywood\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fshawshank-redemption-anniversary-story\"\u003E&quot;a relationship movie for men.&quot;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;Its depiction of prison life was just sanitized enough &#x2014; in comparison to, say, HBO&#x2019;s brutal jail series\u003Cem\u003E Oz\u003C\u002Fem\u003E &#x2014; that it didn&#x2019;t alienate more sensitive audiences.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"1366\" height=\"768\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w1366\u002Fc5c9bf832341bfb0f41279348ad42dc4c08e6368.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere are critical voices out there (such as, it should be said, this writer) who still remain skeptical of the film and who find it to be decent enough, certainly, but also overlong and occasionally mired in motivational-poster platitudes mistaken for profundity (&#x201C;Fear can keep you prisoner: hope can set you free,&#x201D; as the tagline read). Yet even for those of us a little baffled by the cult that&#x2019;s grown around the film, there&#x2019;s little doubt that by the time the film reaches its uplifting conclusion, with \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fmovies\u002F13-things-you-didn-t-c1409949868479\u002Fphoto-the-final-sequence-had-a-different-ending-photo-1409960588381.html\"\u003EAndy and Red on an idyllic Mexican beach\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, it has earned it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWe&#x2019;ve watched Andy and Red endure bitter hardships over 20 years of screen time and nearly two-and-a-half hours of real time, and their eventual victory feels hard won. Tim Robbins \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theguardian.com\u002Ffilm\u002F2004\u002Faug\u002F22\u002Ffilm\"\u003Eonce described\u003C\u002Fa\u003E the film&#x2019;s draw by saying that &#x201C;although not everybody has been in jail, on a deeper, more metaphysical level, many people feel enslaved by their environment, their jobs, their relationships&#x2026;. And \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E is a story about enduring and ultimately escaping from that imprisonment.&#x201D; More than its home video success, or TNT airings, or IMDb status, it is \u003Cem\u003EShawshank\u003C\u002Fem\u003E&apos;s simple, universal message that&#x2019;s helped it become so beloved even 20 years on.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWatch \n\u003Cp\u003EEver since computer-generated imagery, or CGI, was added to the filmmaker&#x2019;s arsenal, it&#x2019;s been easy to spot &#x2013; a flying dragon here, a gigantic explosion there, a Jar-Jar Binks everywhere.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut CGI isn&#x2019;t just used for outlandish effects &#x2013; it&#x2019;s frequently deployed by expert filmmakers to achieve subtle shots that otherwise couldn&#x2019;t be achieved with practical methods. The following 14 scenes all feature examples of CGI that were practically invisible, unless you were in the know&#x2026;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Jurassic Park - Ariana Richards\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"298\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F7b2c1b238b141980af27b1f153bb98fe300900df.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EJurassic Park\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(1993)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Big surprise: dinosaurs aren&#x2019;t real. But we&#x2019;re guessing you knew that. CGI took a quantum leap forward in Spielberg&#x2019;s dino epic, but it wasn&#x2019;t just used for rampaging T-Rexes. The scene in which Lex (Ariana Richards) falls through a roof tile and is almost eaten alive by a raptor was actually performed by a stunt girl, but she looked straight at the camera. Richards&#x2019; face was added in post-production, in a process called digital face replacement. It&#x2019;s a seamless shot that still gets us every time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Forrest Gump - Gary Sinise\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"219\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fbae76b003d34466a2071e93e13b9f447711485e9.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EForrest Gump\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(1994)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Computer graphics are great at adding new elements to scenes, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Farticles.latimes.com\u002F1994-07-10\u002Fentertainment\u002Fca-14048_1_gary-sinise\"\u003Ebut they&#x2019;re equally good at removing things, too\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Though it seems obvious now, we remember watching Gary Sinise&#x2019;s amputee Lieutenant Dan back in &#x2018;94 and wondering how it was possible he &#x201C;got no legs&#x201D;. For a more recent and impressive example of&#xA0; so-called digital erasing, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=-HETfSaA7SE\"\u003Esee Marion Cotillard in \u003Cem\u003ERust &amp; Bone\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Die Hard with a Vengeance - Bruce Willis\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"423\" height=\"582\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w423\u002F2aff1bdd0e28fb49c7865e728cd411470500ba8e.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EDie Hard With A Vengeance\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(1995)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Recall, if you will, the last good \u003Cem\u003EDie Hard\u003C\u002Fem\u003E movie, in particular, the scene in which villain Simon Gruber forces Det. John McClane to travel to Harlem and wear a sign bearing the N-word. Bruce Willis did indeed wear the sandwich board, but to stop anyone from taking offense, the phrase read &#x2018;I Hate Everybody.&#x2019; &#xA0;\u003Cspan\u003EThe epithet&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003Ewas later digitally altered in post-production, with the less objectionable version kept for subsequent network TV broadcasts.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"&quot;Fight\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"271\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fba204eff2104b44d3a6d35e809543be8946e1c41.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EFight Club\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(1999)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E David Fincher is the absolute master of using subtle CGI, and \u003Cem\u003EFight Club\u003C\u002Fem\u003E contains several scenes you&#x2019;d never guess were altered. Entire shots &#x2013; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.empireonline.com\u002Ffeatures\u002Fhistory-of-cgi\u002Fp12\"\u003Elike Edward Norton&#x2019;s apartment exploding\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and the shot of the Starbucks coffee cup in the trashcan &#x2013; were digitally constructed, as was the nude fantasy sequence with Helena Bonham Carter&#x2019;s Marla. She never disrobed on set. There was no set. It was all CGI. Sorry to disappoint you, fellas.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Gladiator &#x2013; Oliver Reed\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F1a70f2ad545313e3e06c51d38156936bb31353ab.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EGladiator\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2000)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Sometimes CGI is used when forces outside the director&#x2019;s control intervene &#x2013; and that includes death. \u003Cem\u003EGladiator\u003C\u002Fem\u003E was, tragically, to be Oliver Reed&#x2019;s last movie, but he hadn&#x2019;t finished shooting his scenes when he died of a heart attack in 1999. Director Ridley Scott, who had used CGI in earlier scenes featuring the Colosseum, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.creativeplanetnetwork.com\u002Fnews\u002Fnews-articles\u002Fdigital-resurrections\u002F382628\"\u003Edecided to apply digital face replacement\u003C\u002Fa\u003E onto an extra for the veteran actor&#x2019;s remaining scenes &#x2014; and Olly&#x2019;s memory was suitably honored.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Spider-Man 2 &#x2013; Alfred Molina\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"209\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fbbb9a1e7751f3d50d366a1a58a891ae438e09f45.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003ESpider-Man 2\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2004)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Director Sam Raimi couldn&#x2019;t have created the best superhero movie ever made without the help of CGI, but along with providing the more whiz-bang sequences, digital effects added a touch of gravitas to some slower scenes. For example, the final graceful shot of a redeemed Doc Ock&#x2019;s body beneath the harbor waters is entirely computer-generated &#x2013; a flawless render of Alfred Molina&#x2019;s face.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Brokeback Mountain CGI\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"274\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F9bbe76efb88b8026165a0e0a994bd00cd0f10d72.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EBrokeback Mountain\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2005)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Just two guys on a mountain, hanging out. Why get computers involved? Well, because director Ang Lee is a perfectionist, and when he wants a shot than nature can&#x2019;t provide, he&#x2019;ll take matters into his own hands. \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=kPw5plmkd6Q\"\u003EMore than a few shots are augmented with computers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, adding mountains in the background, and multiplying the sheep being herded. &#x201C;I wish I could quit you,&#x201D; we imagine Lee whispering to his VFX team.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Blood Diamond &#x2013; Jennifer Connelly\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"212\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Febbae4a982857de41646e9c1d00e94c2831994c5.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EBlood Diamond\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2006)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Sometime after Ed Zwick had completed shooting an emotional scene in which Jennifer Connelly&#x2019;s character receives an important phone call, the \u003Cem\u003EBlood Diamond\u003C\u002Fem\u003E director decided he wanted to pump up the drama by having her cry. Rather than pay for a costly reshoot, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.npr.org\u002Ftemplates\u002Fstory\u002Fstory.php?storyId=7584994\"\u003EZwick opted to have a single tear added digitally\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Zodiac - CGI\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F830a0e5acf795e8805c8bc69d03fcab2f49d9412.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EZodiac\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2007)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E It&#x2019;s everywhere, in practically every scene. David Fincher is a stickler for period detail, and while he can maintain the illusion of 1970s San Francisco through costumes, props and the like, even he can&#x2019;t change the city&#x2019;s skyline. Hence, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=xW2xhBSfFps\"\u003Eseveral background and establishing shots in the crime thriller were digitally constructed\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It worked, and \u003Cem\u003EZodiac\u003C\u002Fem\u003E feels like a period piece, just like he wanted.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Photo description goes here.\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"211\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fee5401dfa51c1b418be4731a80cda608893bbe7a.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EThe Fighter\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2010)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Some crowd scenes were bolstered with digital effects, but one scene caused the visual-effects crew a real headache: Mark Wahlberg holding up a napkin with a girl&#x2019;s phone number on it, which couldn&#x2019;t be shown for legal reasons. Director David O Russell didn&#x2019;t want to use a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fen.wikipedia.org\u002Fwiki\u002F555_%28telephone_number%29\"\u003Ephony 555 prefix\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, so had his VFX team \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.postmagazine.com\u002FPublications\u002FPost-Magazine\u002F2011\u002FJanuary-1-2011\u002FVFX-The-Fighter.aspx\"\u003Ecreate a completely CG napkin\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which was inserted into the final shot. Digital napkins? There are more subtle additions, however, such as the early scene in which Portman&#x2019;s character rubs her hands, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.traileraddict.com\u002Fblack-swan\u002Ffeaturette-vfx-breakdown\"\u003Ewhich are made to look slightly elongated\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, hinting at the grotesque transformation that awaits her later in the film.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"The Change-Up &#x2013; Olivia Wilde\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"333\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F92839dd859dca40e968ed8a69367cc5b2c2e2f98.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003EThe Change-Up\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E &#xA0;(2011)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E Boobs. Leslie Mann had the effects team \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpro.boxoffice.com\u002Farticles\u002F2011-08-director-david-dobkin-talks-the-change-up-cg-boobs-and-returning-to-his-indie-roots?q=emotional\"\u003Egive her CG boobs\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (bigger than the real ones on her request), while Olivia Wilde wore pasties for the camera, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpopwatch.ew.com\u002F2011\u002F07\u002F29\u002Folivia-wilde-nude-fake-cgi\u002F\"\u003Ewhich were later replaced with CG nipples\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Les Miserables - CGI\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"383\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F2082db8a98e7518c0b3f1a1ff9636dc9f389a7f8.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cem\u003ELes Mis&#xE9;rables\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E&#xA0; (2012)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe invisible CGI:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E This is a perfect example of how a slight CGI tweak can make the whole shooting process more bearable.
